Aksum, the Ancient Religious Center, Becomes the Second Target of Attack, and the Northern Front Extends 30 Miles 61

The commander of the northern Italian army frontline in Adua, General De Bono, announced today that the Italian army is now targeting Aksum, the ancient religious center of Abyssinia, as its second destination. Previously, the Albanian army had launched a counterattack from Debrasinna to recapture Adua, and the battle was fierce, but they were eventually repelled. It is reported that the Albanian army suffered heavy casualties, while the Italian army suffered only minor losses due to the bombing by aircraft and artillery and the fierce attacks by tanks and infantry. The defense of Adua's garrison against the Italian army exceeded the Italian army headquarters' estimate by about 24 hours before retreating. After the Italian army occupied it, the surrounding locals raised white flags and surrendered to the Italian army. The Italian army headquarters claimed today that the chief of the Hoya area surrendered to General De Bono in the dark during the attack. When the Albanian army withdrew, they still managed to transport Chen Fen's cannons despite the threat of aircraft. According to today's investigation, the Italian army has occupied more than 2,000 square miles of Albanian territory. (National Telegraph on the 6th)

The Italian front line has now extended to 30 miles, averaging 25 miles within Albanian territory. After Aksum is occupied, the three-way army advancing on Adua may pause for about two weeks to consolidate the front line and transport heavy artillery and reinforcements. There are no official reports on the number of casualties in the Italian army. The reports received here are conflicting and worthless. (National Telegraph on the 6th)

Italian Army's Support is Extremely Difficult, and the Use of Force is Not as Smooth as Initially Expected 62

The Italian army's advance into Abyssinia from Asmara is not as smooth as initially expected. An Italian officer who returned from the front line told a special Reuters correspondent that the major difficulties encountered by the Italian army are hard for outsiders to fully believe. The Italian army is now divided into three routes to invade the same target. They must cope with difficult work. Most of the area passed through is mountainous, so it is extremely difficult to support each other. There are only a few small paths that can pass through the mountains, and there is often a risk of being sniped by the enemy. It is often found that dozens of Albanian soldiers are guarding dangerous passes with only a few machine guns, causing an entire army corps to be unable to move forward for a while. On Sunday, the Italian army encountered the most fierce resistance from the Albanian army in Debrasinna. It is estimated that about 600 Albanian soldiers were killed, wounded, and captured in the battle. (Reuters dispatch on the 7th)

Residents of the Albanian Capital Begin to Evacuate to Avoid Air Raids, the Albanian King Orders Soldiers to Use Guerrilla Tactics, and the Recapture of Hualhual Has Not Been Verified 63

Yesterday, the Italian side in Asmara claimed that Adua had fallen, but according to the Albanian authorities, although the Albanian army is not defending the city, the Italian army has not occupied it. However, the news that the Italian army occupied Adigrat has now been officially acknowledged by the authorities. It is reported that the diplomatic corps stationed outside has requested their respective governments to seek guarantees from Rome that the Albanian capital and Dire Dawa will not be bombed by aircraft, as there are many foreigners residing in both places.

At the same time, the people of the Albanian capital have begun to evacuate. The Albanian King ordered the entire city to dig cellars to avoid air raids. The location is designated on a small hill near the British Embassy outside the capital, as it is unlikely to be bombed by aircraft. Now, residents are helping the old and the young, walking or riding mules to the area, even taking their chickens and dogs with them. In the morning and evening, the entire city will be evacuated. When Italian aircraft attack, there will be no one to be seen except the police.

Personnel from the Italian consulate in Debra Marcos have arrived here after traveling over a hundred miles with a camel team for two weeks. It is expected that Italian Ambassador Count Vinci will ask the Albanian government to issue exit passports. There are five men and one woman in total. They swam 250 yards across the Blue Nile, which was swollen with high water. They encountered seven people who did not cause any trouble.

News from the front line here says that the Albanian army dug deep pits when the Italian army attacked Adua and covered them with green leaves, causing four Italian tanks to fall into the pits, and the people in the tanks were all killed.

The Albanian army on the Wokaden front is still using old tactics, constantly sniping at the vanguard of the Italian army. The Italian army is using aircraft to scout the sky and dropping bombs wherever Albanian soldiers are seen. The reports about the Albanian army recapturing Hualhual are conflicting. The Albanian authorities here solemnly stated that the Albanian army avoided fierce fighting with the Italian army around Adua, following the Albanian King's order last week to only use guerrilla tactics. Therefore, in the Battle of Adua, only the vanguard of the Italian army clashed with the Albanian army's sentry camp. The war in the past four days has had a great psychological impact on the Albanian people, as the Albanian people have never known the ferocity of the new tactics.

The military authorities here now admit that the Italian army is advancing very quickly and has no time to consolidate the land it has gained. (Reuters dispatch on the 7th)

British and French Naval Cooperation in the Mediterranean, but with Three Conditions, and Britain Intensifies Its Defense 65

(London) The British government previously asked France what attitude it would take if the Italian fleet attacked the British fleet in the Mediterranean for no reason. The French government has now replied, saying that any member of the League of Nations that is subjected to aggressive attacks, France is willing to assist its defense with a preparedness plan, but subject to the following three conditions: (1) This preparedness plan should be implemented with mutual consent; (2) It must be implemented simultaneously in the air, on land, and at sea; (3) It must also be implemented in the same way if a non-League of Nations member state invades. (Paris) French jurists today notified the Suez Canal Company that regardless of whether European countries impose sanctions on Italy, the Suez Canal must not be closed to prohibit Italian ships from passing through. According to the Treaty of Constantinople, the Suez Canal must not be prohibited from passing through for ships of any country, nor can it be blockaded. The treaty was also approved by Versailles after the European War. After receiving this notification, the company issued a statement saying, "This company is a commercial organization, so it is in a neutral position. This neutral position was recognized when the canal was approved, so any commercial and military ships can pass through without hindrance." (National Telegraph on the 6th)

It is recognized here that the US President's actions have now completed the following points: (1) Consolidate Britain's position in adopting an effective plan to stop the East African war; (2) The League of Nations can discuss sanctions based on this; (3) Promote the League of Nations to adopt equally strong plans, but only to deal with aggressor countries. Refugees from Pi County Cross the Huai River and Go South 79

Qingjiangpu: In the afternoon of the 7th, about 200 refugees from Hanzhuang, Pi County, including men, women, old and young, were traveling on seven sailboats, passing through Wohe and Huaiyin to the south. Most of them had exposed elbows and looked pale. According to them, it took four days to travel from Pi County to Huaiyin. Along the way, they saw that the water above Xutang had receded day by day, with only a sheet of water remaining. The houses were not visible. The area around Xia Yao Su was in dire straits. The situation south of Liu Laojian was relatively better. They were going to Nanjing to beg for food to prolong their lives. Their words were so sad that those who saw them felt a pang of grief. (Special dispatch on the 7th)

Huang Fu Arrives in Hangzhou to Tour West Lake 80

Hangzhou: Huang Fu and his wife arrived in Hangzhou last night and stayed at Ge Jing'en's residence in Qianwang Temple. On the 7th, they enjoyed a tour of West Lake and visited Xu Qingfu and others. According to them, he came to Hangzhou to visit relatives and friends and had no mission. He will stay in Hangzhou for one or two days and then go to Shanghai for a physical examination. He does not plan to go to Beijing for the time being and made no comment on taking up the post of Minister of Interior. (Special dispatch on the 7th)

What I Saw and Heard in the West: A Glimpse of Wuhan Society 81

— By Our Special Correspondent, Ji Yuan

Hankou is located on the left bank of the Yangtze and Han Rivers. The city has a population of about 800,000 and has always been known as the "Thoroughfare of Nine Provinces" and the "Chicago of the East." In fact, the Thoroughfare of Nine Provinces has almost become a thing of the past. With the development of transportation, the export of goods from west to east can go directly to Shanghai via the Longhai Railway or the Yangtze River, and south to Guangzhou for export, unlike in the past when Hankou was the only distribution center for goods exported from the western, northwestern, and southwestern provinces. As for the "Chicago of the East," it seems to be a bit of an exaggeration. Not to mention other things, just considering the only industrial yarn factories in the Wuhan area, three out of the four factories in the area have closed down, and the only remaining one is also on its last legs. According to investigations, the social situation in Hankou, whether in commerce, finance, or people's livelihoods, is difficult. There are more than 20 banks in Hankou, and the number of money houses has decreased from 70 or 80 in the past to 64 recently and is still gradually decreasing. In recent years, the task of banks and money houses has not been to adjust finance and circulate funds but to concentrate cash and recover debts. What is even stranger is that cash cannot be concentrated, debts cannot be recovered, and credit is frozen to a very high degree. The phenomenon of banks swallowing money houses is like big fish eating small fish. The power that used to be the foundation of Hankou's financial organization has declared its disintegration. According to those familiar with the financial industry, the most obvious example is that Hankou's largest Yuyu Money House declared liquidation at the end of June this year due to excessive pressure from the Bank of Communications. At present, many small money houses with better conditions intend to close down voluntarily. (The minimum capital of Hankou money houses is only 3,000 yuan, and the maximum is less than 100,000 yuan.)

In terms of commerce, the number of shops closing down is indeed not small, and regardless of which business, there is a phenomenon of changing bosses three times within a year, especially Guanghuo shops. Most of those who take over as bosses are creditors or shop owners with more capital and longer-term plans. The most popular saying in the Hankou market is "Only shop assistants are seen, not customers." However, there are also many shops that cannot close down even if they want to. The financial industry does not dare to excessively pressure the debts of various merchants, fearing that once a general bankruptcy trend is formed and all shops declare liquidation, they will also inevitably suffer losses. However, they dare not lend funds again to ask for trouble. Therefore, larger shops are in a dilemma. Since the facts are like this, the number of shops declaring closure is increasing day by day. According to the latest statistics, 20 to 30 Guanghuo shops in the city have posted signs saying "Shopfront is for rent." Among the 20 Nanjing-style grocery stores in the city, 16 have closed down. Along Zhongshan Road, which is the busiest area in Hankou, there are also many empty shops.

Although general commerce is declining day by day, the sales of foreign goods are on the rise. Among them, Japanese goods are the most prominent. According to Mr. Li of the Hankou Commercial Monthly, Hankou is a major base for dumping foreign goods, accounting for about nine-tenths of the city's total trade. Domestic goods trade accounts for only one-tenth. Foreign goods are divided into two categories: Japanese goods and European and American goods. The ratio is six for Japanese loans and four for European and American goods. The annual trade value of Japanese goods is about 30 million yuan or more, and this number is still increasing. The main items of Japanese goods exported to Hankou are textiles and cotton yarn, followed by seafood and medicinal materials. The dumping of Japanese yarn and cloth is the fatal blow to the collapse of Hankou's yarn factory industry, etc. In the past, Hankou had several special phenomena. First, the larger the shop, the more losses it suffered. On the contrary, small businesses could barely survive. Second, large restaurants such as Xinghualou have closed down, while economical restaurants have increased instead. The word "economical" has become a fashionable buzzword. Third, there is a large surplus of labor, with nowhere to sell it, especially among middle and lower-class citizens.

Before the great flood in the 20th year of the Republic of China, the real estate business in Hankou was still in its heyday. Banks, both foreign-owned such as the Banca di Cina and Chinese-owned such as the Shanghai Bank, almost all focused on the real estate business, and their profits were several times higher than lending. The current situation is very different. The real estate business is extremely depressed. Often, several or even dozens of houses are unattended. A second landlord of a three-story building has to pay the entire rent himself. Before the 20th year of the Republic of China, if a second landlord owed the landlord rent for three months, the landlord would file a lawsuit with the court, and the court would issue a strict order to pay the rent within a time limit, otherwise, the landlord would be punished without leniency. Now, rent arrears have reached as many as 28 months. The local court has accumulated more than 1,800 cases of requests for rent recovery. The court is very distressed and has no way to deal with them, so it can only temporarily shelve them and discuss them at length.

After the great flood this year, the social situation is such that there are more than 7 million disaster victims in the province crying for food. The Wuhan authorities have strictly restricted the entry of disaster victims into the city. Therefore, the disaster victims cannot stay in Wuhan. (During the great flood in the 20th year of the Republic of China, the three towns of Wuhan still accommodated 300,000 disaster victims, but recently only 1,000 to 2,000 people have been allowed.) However, these people mostly gather near Wuhan or lead a life of fleeing famine in groups, which still indirectly affects Wuhan's commerce and security. The Wuhan authorities are therefore quite worried and also suffer from the pain of providing only a drop in the bucket in terms of relief. Not long ago, Wuhan held a disaster relief fundraising rally, but the amount raised was less than 40,000 yuan. Compared with the fundraising results of more than 400,000 yuan in the 20th year of the Republic of China, it can be seen that the social economy is becoming increasingly depleted.

Amidst the Sound of Winter Prevention: Bomb Case in Guangzhou Municipality: Bombs Left on Changshou East Road: A Naughty Boy Picks It Up as a Toy: Four Children Seriously Injured After the Explosion 82

Guangzhou Communication: Since the implementation of the district pacification in Guangdong, the public security in various counties and towns has gradually become stable. Recently, with the arrival of winter prevention, various counties and villages have been organizing joint defense, formulating joint defense covenants, helping each other, and reporting bandit tracks by the village chief, making it difficult for petty criminals to hide. If there is a bandit alarm in a locality, the neighboring village guard team must immediately go to support and intercept the bandits. As for the areas where various counties border, inter-provincial defense regulations are mutually agreed upon, joint defense areas are delineated, and in case of an alarm, the police teams in neighboring areas are dispatched to suppress the bandits, regardless of territorial boundaries. Village police who encounter difficulties in suppressing bandits are rewarded and compensated by the joint defense association. The joint defense associations that have been established include the joint defense associations of Xinhui, Taishan, Kaiping, Enping, and Chixi, etc. As for the urban areas, due to the complexity of the local area, the mix of Chinese and foreigners, and the uneven quality of people, the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau has recently been earnestly protecting the public security in Guangzhou Municipality. In recent days, it has increased the number of plainclothes detectives to investigate various public places, cracked down on public and private clubs, and inspected long-distance buses from time to time to check passenger certificates in order to maintain public security. However, despite the strict searches, there are still bandits who are not afraid of the law and smuggle bombs, plotting wrongdoing, resulting in a bomb injuring people on September 30. The incident occurred at 4 pm that day, at the Changqing Xin Street entrance next to the Changshou Public Security Sub-bureau on Changshou East Road in the city. Seven or eight nearby street children were playing together. One of the girls, named Shao Yinhao, caught sight of an abandoned iron can on the street, which was rectangular and about an inch wide. She picked it up as a toy and gathered with the other children to watch. An old woman on the roadside scolded them to put it back where it was. As soon as the object was thrown on the ground, it exploded with a loud noise, and the roof tiles were shaken. Three young children were injured on the spot, and another five children fell to the ground unconscious. The neighbors rushed forward to inspect and saw that the children were either injured or collapsed, and the situation was very tragic. The Changshou Public Security Sub-bureau immediately sent armed police to the scene of the incident to inspect. It was found that the bomb was very powerful, and there were sharp nails scattered inside. At the same time, three circular unexploded bombs were also found under the wall. The bureau immediately reported the case with the exploded and unexploded bombs. On the one hand, the Municipal Hospital was telegraphed to send an ambulance to send the four most seriously injured boys and girls to the hospital for treatment. The injured were identified as Shao Yinhao, 9 years old, from Heshan County, residing at No. 12 Changxing Society nearby, Shao Jianneng (Shao Yinhao's younger brother), 4 years old, Chen Shaolan, 7 years old, from Nanhai County, and Chen Ruilan, 3 years old (Chen Shaolan's younger sister), the children of the Rongji mosquito net shop owner on Changshou Road. After being sent to the hospital, it was found that Shao Yinhao had serious head and back injuries, Shao Jianneng had serious chest injuries, and Chen Shaolan had serious forehead and lung injuries. Due to excessive blood loss, all three were in a coma and feared for their lives. Chen Ruilan was only slightly injured and was discharged from the hospital after applying medicine. (October 1st)

In Wengyuan County, Guangdong: Discovery of the Big Sword Society Bandits: Demonstrations and Parades Slaughter Local Police Officers: Government Troops Arrive to Suppress Them, Scattering to the Borders of San'nan in Jiangxi 83

Guangzhou Communication: The northeast of Guangdong Province is all poor counties with mountainous terrain, and the natives are ignorant and particularly fierce. Therefore, societies that guide people to superstition and secret organizations often incite the ignorant people to plot wrongdoing. Recently, the Changfa Party in Hailufeng in eastern Guangdong and the Big Sword Society in Wengyuan in northern Guangdong are the most famous. After the Changfa Party's unrest was suppressed by the defense army, it has disappeared. However, the Big Sword Society uses Wengyuan and the borders of San'nan in Jiangxi as a gathering place, and it has recently gathered thousands of people. It is found that the Big Sword Society is also known as the Horse Sword Divine Strike Society, and its slogan is to support the weak and eliminate the strong. Its organization is similar to the Yihetuan of the Qing Dynasty. It claims that its members' swordsmanship can resist guns and cannons, and that once the body is trained, even bullets cannot penetrate it. Ten years ago, there were only about 100 members, scattered in Lianping and Xinfeng counties. Later, the organization was expanded, and the party members gathered in Wengyuan. Each of the party members was equipped with a long sword, about three feet long, flashing light to demonstrate to the ignorant people. The members of the association wore yellow lower garments as a sign. Those who joined the association paid an annual membership fee of 12 yuan and could get the protection of the Big Sword Society. In recent years, the number of people has increased, and they have engaged in strict organization, setting up branch associations in the second, fifth, and sixth districts of Wengyuan. A part of them is stationed in San'nan on the border of Jiangxi, calling themselves the Heavenly Kingdom Army, and supporting Li Tianbao as the commander-in-chief and Zhong Riying as the commander-in-chief. They made fixed numbers of flags and banners. The flag is square, with a white sun in the middle, blue above and red below. As the number of party members of the Big Sword Society increased day by day, they became more rampant in the spring of this year. The people in the third district of Wengyuan presented a request to the government to ban them because the gangsters were rampant. The county government issued a notice prohibiting the gathering of the Divine Strike Team. The Big Sword Society believed that the local self-defense force in the border area was weak and that the county army's power was also insufficient. Therefore, on September 9, it gathered 500 to 600 members of the association and held a demonstration parade in the third district, issuing various slogans to incite the people. The county government then reported the situation to the Northwest District Pacification Department. After receiving the report, the Pacification Department dispatched a company of soldiers led by Battalion Commander Feng of the Independent Third Brigade stationed in the county on September 13 to suppress the Bazi area of the third district, ordering the Big Sword Divine Strike Team to sign a bond to disband. The defense army also returned to its original defense. The gangsters were angered by the local officials and resented the local officials. However, they suddenly gathered nearby gangs to besiege Longxian City in the third district of Wengyuan, slaughtering Zhang Zuomin, the patrol officer of the local public security station, and several merchants, looting more than 1,000 yuan in cash, and seizing more than ten rifles from the guards. Then they attacked Nanpu Market in the third district and Gangwei Market in the sixth district. On September 23, the Northwest Pacification Department urgently dispatched the first and second battalions of the Teaching Regiment of the Fourth Division stationed in Yingde County and Liao Daoming's troops of the Eleventh Regiment stationed in Maba to cooperate with the county soldiers to suppress the bandits. The Northwest Pacification Department also sent Councilor Zhang and Judge Feng to the county to direct everything. Each unit advanced towards the second and sixth districts. The Big Sword Team knew that they could not resist, and part of them fled to Lianping and Xinfeng, and part of them fled to the border of Jiangxi. The government troops carried out both suppression and appeasement, and those who were coerced were not punished. More than 1,000 big swords and dozens of inferior guns were seized in the three, five, and six districts of Wengyuan. At the moment, a part of the Fourth Division is stationed there to intimidate and urge local officials to rush to handle the aftermath, investigate the household registration, and compile and train the Baojia system to prevent future troubles. (October 3rd)

The Jiangxi Pacification Department is Abolished: The Unfinished Matters of Qingxiang Aftermath: Handled by the Provincial Government and Garrison Troops 84

Nanchang Communication: After Chairman Chiang entered Sichuan to supervise the suppression of the Communist bandits, he established the Pacification Commissioner's Office in Jiangxi and appointed Gu Zhutong as the Director of Pacification to handle the elimination of the remaining bandits and local aftermath to complete the task of Qingqiang. When the Pacification Commissioner's Office was established, it divided the entire province into eight pacification zones, and Tan Daoyuan, Zhao Guantao, and others were appointed as directors of the pacification zones in each zone. All the remaining small groups in various places were successively wiped out. The bandit leaders who remained in Jiangxi and had not fled, such as Fang Zhimin, Gao Yongsheng, and Xu Yangang, were either captured alive or killed. In the future, only local troops will need to take on the task of searching and guarding. Therefore, the central government believes that the pacification work in Jiangxi Province has reached a considerable level, so on the 3rd, it issued a clear order to abolish the Jiangxi Provincial Pacification Commissioner's Office. Director Gu Zhutong was transferred to the post of Director of the Sichuan Provisional Headquarters of the Military Commission. After the Jiangxi Provincial Pacification Commissioner's Office received the order of abolition, the Chief of Staff, Dian Qingzhu, asked for instructions on the closing method. All the unfinished matters of Qingxiang aftermath will be handled by the provincial government and the local garrison troops.

Fujian Province Implements Austerity: Administrative Construction and Judiciary All Reduce Political Power: At the Same Time, It Plans to Hold Two New Taxes 85

Fuzhou Newsletter: Due to financial difficulties, Fujian Province has implemented austerity measures. The merger of all provincial district administrative inspector commissioners, the reform of the organization of county governments, the salary reduction of civil servants, and the abolition of road engineering offices were all implemented on October 1. After the District Administrative Inspector Commissioner's Office was merged from ten districts into seven districts, the expenses of each district were fixed at 5,000 yuan per month (including the expenses of the security headquarters and the county government where it is located). After the reform of the county government, only three departments were set up. All public security bureaus, education bureaus, road construction associations, and construction associations were abolished. After the salary reduction of civil servants, except for police officers and workers, all salaries were reduced by 10%. If the total amount of the discount is less than one-tenth of the agency's fixed expenses, staff should be laid off or public expenses should be reduced to make up for it. After the cancellation of the engineering offices in each section, only the road construction team was retained to complete the unfinished road work and repair the damaged roads. In addition, the provincial party affairs expenses were also reduced from more than 310,000 yuan per year to more than 260,000 yuan. Now, the provincial party affairs commissioner's office believes that the number of staff in the provincial party headquarters has been reduced and cannot be reduced further, so it has decided to reduce salaries. It is likely to follow the example of administrative agencies and reduce them by 10%. The salaries of party headquarters in each county cannot be reduced further, so it is decided to reduce staff again. Generally, each county used to have two instructors, but now only one is retained. In addition, the Higher Court used to have a three-level, three-trial system and had decided to set up higher branch courts in important areas and local courts in prosperous counties. However, due to financial difficulties and the inability to increase funding, the establishment of other courts will be postponed except for those that have already been opened and will be discussed again next year. Due to the impact of the reduction in political power, the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau will reduce the size of the Health Department and the Fire Brigade. However, the largest expenditure in the province is for the security team, which costs 300,000 yuan per month in total. A few days ago, Zhao Nan, the director of the Security Department, flew to Zhangzhou to discuss with Chiang Dingwen, the director of pacification, to reduce the number of troops by one-third, and the military expenditure can also be reduced to 200,000 yuan. It is likely that the downsizing can be implemented from November. As for the new taxes that the provincial government plans to hold, there are two types: one is the housing tax, which has been formulated into regulations and promulgated for implementation in various counties. A tax of 3% is levied according to the amount of rent, which can generate 2 million yuan per year. The other is the donation of superstitious goods (candles, firecrackers, incense, and foil), which has been decided by the Provincial Government Committee to open, and a donation of 30% is levied according to the price of the goods, which can generate 1 million yuan per year to make up for the financial deficit. (October 5)

Yuehan Railway Committee Meeting: Discuss and Decide on the Traffic Plan: All Committee Members Will Participate in the Zhuzhou-Hengyang Traffic Ceremony 86

Hankou Communication: The Yuehan Railway Consolidation Planning Committee of the Ministry of Railways, in order to plan the traffic of the entire line, held the second plenary session of the committee on the 3rd at the Xiang'e Railway Bureau. A total of Chairman Xia Guangyu, counselor of the Ministry of Railways, committee member Ling Hongxun, director of the Zhushao section, Li Xiangen, director of the Guangshao section, Yin Deyang, director of the Xiang'e section, special committee member Huang Boqiao, director of the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Bureau, Bian Xiaoxian, assistant of the Ministry of Railways Engineering Department, Chen Yaozu, director of the Ministry of Railways Finance Department, Zou Anzhong, deputy director of the Pinghan Railway, Chen Qingwen, director of the Xiang'e Railway Transportation Department, Zhu Qidian, Tan Peiran, technicians Xia Anshi, Secretary Ma Tingshe, Deng Sixiong, Gao Lunjin, chief auditor of the Zhushao section, and consultants Luo Lu, Feng Lehou, and other important personnel of each road, more than 200 people attended. There were eight proposals from the financial group, one from the road affairs group, nine from the transportation group, seven from the engineering group, four from the mechanical group, three from Xia Guangyu, and four from the committee members. After the conference on the 3rd, the review was conducted separately on the 4th, and the conference was continued on the 5th. It closed on the evening. Plans have been agreed upon on matters such as completing the traffic of the entire line, consolidating debts, opening customs terminals, and intermodal transport across the river. On the 6th, the committee members jointly proposed the entire proposal, and it was decided to take a special car to Hunan on the 7th to inspect the engineering along the road. It is planned to inspect Yuezhou Station on the 8th, arrive in Hengzhou on the 9th, participate in the traffic ceremony of the Zhuzhou-Hengyang section on the 10th, continue to depart on the 11th, and rush to Guangzhou around the 15th. According to Xia Guangyu's talk about the mission of the conference, the Yuehan Railway starts from Wuchang in the north and reaches Guangzhou in the south. It is an important trunk line in southern China. After the establishment of the National Government, it paid attention to the completion of the entire line. This time, the headquarters borrowed Sino-British Boxer Indemnity to complete the unfinished project of Zhushao section, which cost a lot of effort. In the future, after the traffic is opened, the principal and interest must be fulfilled on schedule and credit must be established. Then, the funds required for the construction of new roads in the future can be raised by law. Therefore, its relationship to the future of road administration is extremely important. In order to achieve this goal, the road must have a reliable surplus every year after the entire line is opened to traffic, so that it can be used to repay the principal and interest of the debt on schedule. The most important mission of this conference is to plan the traffic of the entire line and the subsequent development of business, so that the business income, in addition to road maintenance, is sufficient to repay the principal and interest. Therefore, the transportation, organization, engineering, mechanical affairs, and finance of the road after the completion of the unification are all related and must be consolidated and planned in advance, etc. (6th)

Ms. Liu Manqing: Three Trips to Tibet: —Has Now Returned to the Capital— 87

Ms. Liu Manqing was previously specially appointed by the Central Government to go to Tibet twice to convey its intentions and conduct investigations. Recently, Ms. Liu went to Tibet alone again, and few outsiders knew about it. When Ms. Liu passed through Hankou, she met the female aviator Ms. Lin Pengxia. Because they took the same ship to Yichang, they changed to a car to Chengdu and then entered Tibet via Dajianlu. Along the way, she changed her attire, hired only one worker, and carried simple luggage. The round trip was tens of thousands of miles, and she was not afraid of hardship. It is heard that Ms. Liu's trip was due to the death of her maternal grandmother, and her filial piety is especially commendable. It is now known that Ms. Liu has completed the funeral and has now returned to the capital.

Changzhou Detective Dies from Severe Injuries Sustained During Arrest 89

Nine detectives, including Zhou Yiwen, from the Wuyi County Public Security Bureau's Detective Squad, were ordered by County Magistrate Hou Houzong to cross the border to Shizhuang in the Seventh District of Jiangyin County to arrest four bandits, including Peng Shengrong. The county government forwarded the report to the District Court Procuratorate, which dispatched personnel to conduct an examination on the morning of the 7th. According to news from Jiangyin, since the incident occurred, Shizhuang Town has experienced several nights of alarm. Local figures have requested that District Chief Shen travel to the Jiangyin County government to request the dispatch of a platoon of security guards to the town for suppression.

Local News

Suggestions for Curtailing Expenditures: Taxpayers' Association Forwards Letter to the Public Works Department and Replies to Executive Committee Members for Information 91

The Shanghai Public Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association's executive committee members Xu Xiaochu, Jin Zongcheng, and others recently sent a letter to the association requesting that the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department be advised to curtail expenses and that the Shanghai Telephone Company should not increase prices. In addition to forwarding the letter to the Public Works Department for consideration, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association also replied to the committee members yesterday, stating: "We received your letter of September 28 on October 2, requesting advice regarding the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department, etc., to curtail expenses. We have taken note of everything, and we deeply admire your concern for public welfare. This association has anticipated the economic decline for the past five years and has repeatedly warned the Public Works Department regarding its finances. In particular, on November 10, 1931, we sent a letter to the Public Works Department, stating: 'Government organs, whether central or local, have a fixed financial policy. Before the European War, government finances were based on the policy of 'measuring expenditures by income.' Afterward, the opposite was true, with the policy of 'measuring income by expenditures.' Furthermore, the implementation of financial policies must take into account the economic capacity of taxpayers. It is imperative that private economics are not insufficient while public economics are overly abundant. If the two cannot be balanced, it is better for the private sector to be sufficient than for the public sector to be. Moreover, 'to achieve the greatest effect with the least amount of expenditure' is the highest principle of economics, and both public and private economics must adhere to it as a standard. This should be well known to the authorities. Since the European War, the finances of the defeated countries have indeed been strained, and even the finances of the victorious countries have been stretched thin. In fact, after the European War, countries around the world have suffered from financial panic. In recent years, the stagnation of commerce has greatly affected the public and private economics of various countries. As a result, Japan has adopted austerity policies, the United States has postponed war debts for one year, and the British Labor Cabinet has collapsed due to an unbalanced budget and has been replaced by a national government that is tightening its budget to overcome difficulties. It is evident that government finances must take into account the state of world commerce and the national economy and cannot arbitrarily expand without considering economy. Shanghai is the economic center of China and the eastern hub of world trade. However, Shanghai is only a distribution center for commerce, and Shanghai's commerce relies entirely on the Yangtze River basin, and to a lesser extent on northern and southern China. The Yangtze River basin has suffered the worst floods in China's history in sixty years, and since the Eastern Provinces have been invaded by Japanese forces, trade with Shanghai has come to a standstill. Those who live in Shanghai, in addition to spending heavily on disaster relief, have also lost profits in commerce. Therefore, what is their state of distress? The recent vacancy of new rental properties, with no one responding, is enough to understand the reason. The once bustling western section of Hankou Road is now often closed, which is enough to prove the beginning of the market's decline. Based on the above circumstances, the Public Works Department's financial policy should focus on economy rather than simply seeking to increase revenue to maintain budget equilibrium. This is the common opinion of the citizens. The Association, considering the decline of world commerce, the stagnation of national trade, and the gradual decline of the market, hereby requests that the Public Works Department implement large-scale economic austerity measures and pay particular attention to curtailing administrative expenses and suspending unnecessary projects. Furthermore, there are two types of municipal expenditures: active and passive. Capital expenditures for municipal public utilities fall into the former category because they are productive expenses. Education expenditures, on the other hand, fall into the latter category because their effects are slower to materialize and cannot be measured numerically. However, it can be asserted that any attempt to reduce them will harm both society and the nation. In addition, police and sanitation expenses should be listed separately. The amount of these expenses should be proportional to the effectiveness of the services. For example, if the number of crimes increases, the cost of defense and policing must be expanded. However, whether the expansion is appropriate depends on whether the number of crimes decreases. If the cost of defense and the number of crimes increase simultaneously, this would be a great departure from economic principles. Therefore, the appropriateness of these expenses depends solely on the effectiveness of the services. The Association has the following four suggestions for economy. If adopted, they will help to alleviate the Public Works Department's budget deficit for the coming year. According to the report of the Director of Administration, the expenditure items in the 1932 budget will exceed the revenue items by a staggering 2.9 million taels. 1. The music band (annual cost of 190,000 taels) should be disbanded directly or reorganized under private management, as this is not an essential municipal undertaking. Moreover, it is unfair to use public funds to provide cheap entertainment for a small number of people. 2. Defense expenditures currently account for 39 percent of the Public Works Department's total revenue. However, if more senior staff are replaced with Chinese personnel, significant savings can be achieved in terms of salaries. This applies not only to the Police Department but also to other administrative departments. The Association has repeatedly asked the Public Works Department to pay attention to the employment of senior Chinese personnel, primarily for the purpose of saving expenses. If the Public Works Department can employ more Chinese personnel, the "exchange rate tightening" and "subsidy" items in the current budget can be greatly reduced, resulting in substantial savings. 3. Public works expansion is proceeding too rapidly, and the expenditure on road expansion and other projects is substantial. If economy can be implemented, it will greatly benefit the Public Works Department's finances. The Association is well aware that road improvement is closely related to municipal development and can increase land values along the roads, thereby increasing the department's tax revenue. However, as land values increase, rents will also rise, which will significantly affect the cost of living for citizens. Road expansion is not only a short-term plan but also a long-term strategy. Therefore, the workload should be distributed over several years and gradually constructed. It should not be rushed to achieve immediate results, which would cause any given year's budget to suffer from uneven revenue. 4. Staff salaries should be excellent to attract talented and dedicated staff. However, there are many positions that do not require large salaries to fill. This was suggested by the Economic Committee but has not yet been fully implemented. While the monthly salary of a patrolman is not sufficient to provide security in the current cost of living, the monthly salary of the highest-ranking official is 140 times higher, excluding allowances. British Prime Minister MacDonald recently reduced his annual salary by 1,000 pounds, which could be emulated. The above four points are merely the most prominent. In summary, the expenditure for productive enterprises should not be spared, and the expenditure for improving citizens' knowledge should not be spared, but the focus should be on practicality rather than superficial aesthetics. Taxes that contribute to the increase in crime should be reduced as much as possible. As it concerns the key to the city's prosperity and decline, we are sending this letter for your consideration and prompt implementation.'" Regarding the issue of telephone price increases, we sent a letter to the Public Works Department Board on September 6, stating: "Regarding the issue of the Shanghai Telephone Company's price increase, we are pleased that the Board has temporarily approved an 11% price increase and has, in accordance with the resolution of the Taxpayers' Association, hired experts to conduct research. However, we believe that the scope of the Board's research is too narrow, and the results will inevitably be detrimental to the taxpayers and beneficial to the Shanghai Telephone Company. In order to avoid the Board being suspected of favoring the Shanghai Telephone Company and neglecting the public interest, the Association submitted the case to the Executive Committee meeting on September 3, which resolved that the Board should be asked to expand the scope of expert research for the following reasons: (1) The object of research should be the entirety of the Shanghai Telephone Company. (2) The largest expenditures of the Shanghai Telephone Company are the annual interest of shareholders and reserves, the 4.5% operating revenue subsidy to the International Electric Materials Company, the 5% commission on the purchase of materials, and the income tax paid by the company. (3) If the Shanghai Telephone Company does not use the Haishen method when purchasing materials to avoid changes in exchange rates, the losses caused by these changes will be very large. Therefore, the scope of research should be expanded to include the following three points: (1) The interest rates of telephone businesses around the world are far different from the interest rate of the Shanghai Telephone Company. The Shanghai Telephone Company's 6% debentures were issued in Shanghai and are not excessive. Is it reasonable to have a dividend of 8% and a reserve of 2%, totaling 10%? If not, provide a reasonable interest rate. (2) Operating revenue subsidies, material purchase commissions, and income tax should be paid from operating expenses. (3) Are there ways to avoid losses due to exchange rate fluctuations? Whose fault is it? Should the public compensate for it? If the above three items are not included, any research within other scopes will not have the maximum effect of reducing the burden on the public. We are sending this letter for your consideration and implementation." On September 17, we sent another letter to the Board, stating: "On September 6, we requested that the Board expand the scope of the telephone expert research to include three items. We trust that you have noted and implemented them. We hereby solemnly declare to the Board that if the scope of research is not expanded, the Association will not consider the research report satisfactory, and there is room for consideration regarding the wishes of telephone users. Please pay special attention to this matter. We are sending this letter for your consideration." We have forwarded the above letters to the Public Works Department and stated that the letter covers two points: (1) The Public Works Department should strive to curtail expenses. (2) The Shanghai Telephone Company should not increase prices. Regarding the first point, the Association has repeatedly warned against Shanghai becoming a continuation of Chicago for the past five years and sent a letter to the Public Works Department on November 10, 1931, requesting that it implement austerity policies. We are now sending a copy of the translation for your reference. We also anticipate that the number of vacant houses will increase daily and rents will decrease daily. If the general tax is collected as before, the amount will decrease daily. Therefore, in 1933, the Taxpayers' Representatives' Assembly resolved to collect the general tax on vacant houses, but we do not know the reason why the Public Works Department has ignored this resolution. Instead, it wants to use the valuation power, which has long been replaced by custom, on the basis of "actual rent" to increase rent and increase the actual general tax. Furthermore, it has established a committee with no basis in fundamental law and paid a member a large subsidy in exchange for confidential documents. This is actually a contradictory measure that promotes rent increases and increases the public burden. Furthermore, it has delayed the established eight-year education plan. Why is it necessary to establish a car committee when the Public Works Department's Traffic Division can handle public rickshaws, which only generates over 200,000 yuan in revenue annually? Therefore, we are very dissatisfied with the Public Works Department's failure to economize on public funds. Regarding the second point, the Association has explained it in two letters on September 6 and September 17. Please consider them carefully. This is our sincere hope." We are sending this reply for your consideration.

City Chamber of Commerce Writes to Telephone Expert Committee Requesting Cancellation of Toll Calls. Forcing Citizens Citywide to Bear Redundant Costs. Revise Contract Quickly to Achieve Equitable Reason. 92

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has once again sent a letter to the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department Telephone Expert Committee, requesting the cancellation of toll calls between the Chinese and Concession areas, stating: "We, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Concession, have repeatedly detailed the impropriety of charging for calls between the Chinese and Concession areas and believe that the Committee is aware that this should be cancelled. Now, all citizens of the city believe that since all telephones in the Chinese and Concession areas are now equipped with automatic switchboards, and since the distances between the South Shanghai and Zhabei areas and the Concession are short, direct calls are possible without obstruction. However, the Concession Telephone Company inserts manual switchboards in the middle of the lines to record the calls for billing purposes, which forces all citizens to pay redundant fees for the same tool. What could be more improper than this? To correct this impropriety, the toll calls should be cancelled and replaced with direct calls, and the temporary contract between the two parties should be revised as soon as possible to achieve equitable reason and eliminate the citizens' disappointment with the Telephone Company. The Committee stands in an impartial position on this matter and will surely adopt this and provide all our citizens with a satisfactory correction. We are sending this letter for your consideration and approval of revision to show fairness. We sincerely hope for this."

Zhang Fakui Discusses Future Actions. Whether to Do Business or Enter Officialdom, I Hope to Benefit the Country. If Our Country Wants to Become Prosperous and Strong, We Must Promote Industry. 95

Central Committee Member Zhang Fakui, after resigning from his military post, traveled abroad to inspect the industries of various countries. After returning to China this spring, he went to various provinces in the Northwest for inspection. He returned to Shanghai from his travels on the morning of the 6th. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Zhang at his residence yesterday morning. According to him, his impressions of the trip and his future actions are as follows:

Denies Going to Russia

Zhang first denied the news published in the Shanghai foreign newspapers that Director Wang would send Zhang to Russia, saying, "During my travels in the West, a local journalist asked me about this, and I immediately denied it. Although I met with Director Wang once after returning to China, we did not discuss the matter, nor did I hear that the Central Government intended to send anyone to Russia. In short, such reports are purely speculation and should not be believed." Zhang continued, "I am currently a private citizen, and rumors that the Central Government will give me an important position are also untrue. In the future, whether I do business or enter officialdom, I will be brave and willing to do whatever can benefit the Chinese people."

Investigating the People's Suffering

Zhang continued to describe his impressions of the trip, saying, "I was previously a soldier, fighting day and night, and I was unable to thoroughly investigate the suffering of the people in various places at the time. Looking back, I am filled with regret. Since resigning from my military post, I have traveled abroad and then to various provinces in Shandong, Hebei, Shanxi, Shaanxi, and Gansu. The local authorities provided me with excellent hospitality, so my journey was very convenient. However, I learned that merchants and travelers found it extremely difficult to travel. The improvement of transportation in the northwestern provinces, which are important border areas, is a matter of urgency. I had intended to go to Qinghai, but I had to cancel the trip due to the inconvenience of transportation."

Not Leaving Shanghai for the Time Being

"After traveling, I decided to rest for a while and do not plan to leave Shanghai for the time being. However, I will visit provinces and cities that I have not yet visited. Based on what I have learned from this inspection, although our country is based on agriculture, we should strive for rural revitalization, but we should also strive to promote industry in order to survive in the modern world. In this 20th century, all countries are striving for industry. Italy was also based on agriculture, but since 1919, it has strived to promote industry and has become an industrial country. The Soviet Union has also gradually become prosperous and strong after years of striving for industry. Therefore, if our country wants to become prosperous and strong, we should pay attention to this. Although I have this intention, I do not have the strength to do so. Rumors that I will establish an industrial company and raise shares to operate it are also false. In short, my heart is willing, but my strength is insufficient. I hope the Chinese people will pay attention to this," he said.

Cheng Tianfang Lectures on the Italian-Ethiopian War. The Future Trend Will Not Go Beyond Three Paths. China Hopes to Be Spared Expansion. 96

Jiaotong University President Li Zhaohuan hosted a farewell banquet at the school yesterday afternoon for the newly appointed ambassador to Germany, Cheng Tianfang, and invited the deans of various colleges to attend. Before lunch, Ambassador Cheng also gave a lecture to all students at the school's commemorative week, describing the course of the Italian-Ethiopian conflict and predicting that its future outcome would not go beyond three paths: (1) Ethiopia fails early due to insufficient military equipment; (2) a compromise solution is reached after the outbreak of hostilities; (3) various countries are drawn into the vortex, causing a second world war. Given China's weak position, it is hoped that the third situation will not occur. However, even if the Italian-Ethiopian war does not escalate, various countries will inevitably compete to expand their naval, land, and air forces in preparation for a second world war. However, if the various countries can agree on new methods of cooperation, then that would be a different matter, he said.

Shen Chang to Set Sail Tomorrow 103

Shen Chang, the director of the Ping-Sui Railway Administration, was dispatched by the Ministry of Railways to Europe, India, and Japan to investigate railways. He is scheduled to depart from Shanghai tomorrow morning (the 9th) aboard the Italian ship Conte Verde to go abroad. He will first go to India to conduct research for a month, and then go to Europe. Yesterday, reporters interviewed him to inquire about the mission abroad, his achievements in Ping-Sui, and his thoughts on the economic problems of North China. He answered each question as follows: 1. The most important things to pay attention to during this trip abroad are: A. The problem of centralized management of railways. B. The method of borrowing materials for new railways and consolidating old debts. Particular attention will be paid to the precedents of Turkey and Soviet Russia. C. The purchase and management of materials. D. The independence of accounting and the auditing system. E. The appointment, management, and relationship between political parties and railway administration of personnel. Attention will be paid to the current situations in Germany and Italy. 2. I was in Ping-Sui for two and a half years, which coincided with the time when the central authority reached its peak, so I was able to obtain the support of local governments. All department heads were personally selected by Minister Gu, and were the best of the time. Therefore, it was possible to achieve: A. Regardless of the station or time, passengers and goods could be transported out within five days after reporting. B. Regardless of the passenger, there was an opportunity to ride in passenger cars similar to those on the Beijing-Shanghai line every day. C. Ninety-five percent of the old debts have been consolidated and can be repaid on time according to the contract. However, these are the minimum qualifications of the railway, and future development and improvement require even more effort. 3. When I was in Ping-Sui, I focused on railway affairs, and I am ashamed to say that I have no research on general economics. I rarely interacted with Japanese military and civilian officials and visiting experts. People such as Umezu, Shibayama, and Sakai were only seen in the newspapers. Therefore, I am ashamed to say that I cannot answer the so-called economic problems of North China. However, based on common sense, the situation in Europe is becoming increasingly urgent and will inevitably affect Asia. North China will bear the brunt of it. This is truly the autumn of crisis and survival, and so on.

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Compiled and Printed "Answers to Questions Regarding Opium Smoker Registration" and Distributed Them to Various Branch Bureaus for Distribution to Citizens. 104

Since the Municipal Public Security Bureau began carrying out opium smoker registration, the process has been proceeding very smoothly. Although registered opium smokers are very enthusiastic, because the population of this city is so large, it is feared that there are still people who do not understand the meaning of registration and are hesitant to register. Therefore, the bureau has specially compiled and printed "Answers to Questions Regarding Opium Smoker Registration" and distributed them to the bureau's various branch bureaus for distribution to citizens. The content of the Q&A explains the meaning of opium smoker registration in this city without leaving anything out. A New Voice News Agency reporter has recorded the original text of the Q&A as follows: (1) (Question) Why is it necessary to carry out opium smoker registration? (Answer) The meaning of opium smoker registration carried out by this bureau is to clarify the total number of opium smokers and the amount of opium smoked in this city, so as to provide a standard for annual reduction. (2) (Question) Why is it necessary to obtain a opium-cessation license? (Answer) Because the government is considerate of a group of elderly, weak, and deeply addicted opium smokers who cannot immediately quit opium, it has specially formulated a flexible measure to issue opium-cessation licenses to allow such opium smokers to temporarily smoke opium and gradually reduce their consumption. (3) (Question) What are the benefits of opium smokers registering in accordance with the regulations? (Answer) Opium smokers who register in accordance with the regulations are showing that they are obeying government orders. The government allows them to quit opium for free or quit opium gradually within a specified period of two months, so that they will not violate the prohibition. (4) (Question) When does the deadline for voluntary registration expire? (Answer) From July to the end of September of this year is the deadline for voluntary registration. Now, this bureau is extending the deadline by one month because there are still some opium smokers in this city who do not understand the registration procedures. After the end of opium smokers' voluntary registration at the end of October, opium smokers will be arrested, fined, and forced to register. (5) (Question) What are the registration procedures during the period of forced registration? (Answer) During the period of forced registration, this bureau will stop opium smokers from voluntarily registering. Opium addicts who are caught smoking opium in private will be fined from 50 yuan to 300 yuan in accordance with the regulations, and then forced to register. (6) (Question) How will all opium smokers who have not registered in accordance with the regulations after the registration deadline expires be dealt with? (Answer) The registration deadline is stipulated to be the end of this year. After that, this bureau will regard opium smokers who are caught smoking opium in private as opium addicts, and will impose a fine and then send them to a opium-cessation facility for forced rehabilitation. (7) (Question) How many types of limited-time opium-cessation licenses are there, how much do they cost, and how long is the time limit? (Answer) Ordinary limited-time opium-cessation licenses cost 5 yuan. Limited-time opium-cessation licenses for the poor cost only 6 jiao. There is also a travel permit for license holders that costs 3 yuan. Limited-time opium-cessation licenses are valid for six months and must be renewed once. Travel permits expire after three months. After expiration, an application must be made to the local opium prohibition agency for renewal. (8) (Question) If a person who is not poor obtains a opium-cessation license for the poor, will they be punished? (Answer) If it is determined that a person who obtains a opium-cessation license for the poor is not poor, they should be required to obtain an ordinary license and fined twice or five times the cost of the ordinary license. The guarantor will also be fined half of the amount fined to the applicant. (9) (Question) Is it necessary to pay an additional fee to renew a license? (Answer) This bureau plans to adopt the principle of not charging additional fees for license renewal. The first license renewal costs 5 yuan, and the first license also costs 5 yuan. After submitting it to the municipal government for approval, a public announcement will be made. (10) (Question) How can citizens apply for opium cessation? (Answer) The Shanghai North and Shanghai South opium-cessation hospitals have now been established by the Health Bureau. During the voluntary registration period, opium smokers who request opium cessation must fill out an application form and a guarantee form, which can be obtained from the bureau's various branch bureaus. After investigation by this bureau, they will be sent to the opium-cessation hospital for free treatment. When discharged from the hospital, they should fill out a written pledge not to smoke again and file it for future reference. (11) (Question) What should be done if an opium smoker relapses after opium cessation? (Answer) If an opium smoker relapses after opium cessation, after investigation by this bureau or after being reported by someone, this bureau will detain them and transfer them to the local court for punishment in accordance with the law. (12) (Question) How should an opium smoker who voluntarily quits opium prove it and report it to this bureau for filing? (Answer) It is legal for opium smokers to voluntarily quit opium. However, in order to prevent cunning people from using self-cessation as a pretext to evade obtaining a license and secretly continuing to smoke opium, opium smokers who apply for self-cessation do not have to register for a license, but they must quit opium within one month. A certificate proving opium cessation issued by a hospital designated by the Health Bureau must be submitted, along with a pledge not to smoke again, and filed for future reference for random inspections. If this bureau believes that there is still a possibility of fraud, it may still be sent to the opium-cessation hospital for inspection. If it is proven that they are addicted, they will be punished in the same way as those who relapsed after opium cessation after being sent by this bureau. (13) (Question) How should cases of illegally transporting opium and illegally setting up opium dens for people to smoke be punished? (Answer) Cases of illegal transportation and illegal sales that are discovered will be sent to the military law organs for military law punishment, and all their property will be confiscated in accordance with the regulations. In addition, if citizens of this city exchange their opium-cessation licenses, they will be charged additional fees in accordance with the Jiangsu Province method. For example, the first time an opium-cessation license is issued, it costs 6 yuan. The second time the license is exchanged, the fee increases to 12 yuan. The third time, it costs 18 yuan. The purpose of the province's adoption of this method is to increase the fees so that opium smokers can make up their minds to quit opium because they cannot afford to bear the pain. However, this city is adjacent to the concessions. If the Jiangsu Province method is followed, opium smokers who cannot afford to pay will inevitably use the concessions as a refuge. Therefore, citizens of this city believe that this city will also increase fees in accordance with the Jiangsu Province method when exchanging licenses. Therefore, even those with the economic ability to exchange for ordinary opium-cessation licenses come to receive opium-cessation licenses for the poor. The majority are hesitant to exchange their licenses. In view of this situation, in order to alleviate the people's hardship, the bureau plans to adopt a method of not increasing fees for exchanges. Ordinary licenses cost 5 yuan, and licenses for the poor cost 6 jiao. The plan has been submitted to the municipal government for approval. Once the municipal government approves it, a public announcement will be made and it will be implemented.

Ministry of Finance Approves That No Stamp Duty Is Required for Tobacco and Alcohol Licenses 106

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce previously sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance to request instructions on whether or not stamp duty was required for tobacco and alcohol business licenses. Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance issued approval No. Shui Zi 7340, stating: "We have received your presentation stating that tobacco and alcohol business licenses are certificates issued by government agencies for the collection of taxes. In accordance with Article 3 of the Stamp Tax Law, stamp duty is not required. You are hereby informed of this approval."

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Requests a Thorough Investigation of the Xuchang Tobacco Company in Henan Province. This Involves Foreign Businesses Setting Up Factories in Disguise in the Interior. Once This Precedent Is Set, Treaties Will Be Rendered Meaningless. 107

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry to thoroughly investigate whether the Xuchang Tobacco Company in Henan Province is nominally Chinese-owned but actually foreign-owned, and to strictly prevent this. (The previous content is omitted.) In recent years, foreign businesses have often used the names of Chinese people as their managers in order to deceive people because treaties restrict them from setting up factories and businesses in the interior. The fact that the International Savings Society has set up branches all over the interior is an example of this tactic. According to the letter, the association believes that this matter is of great importance and has sent personnel to conduct investigations. According to Mr. Shen Weiting, the chairman of the Chinese Cigarette Factory Industry Association, the Xuchang Company was organized by Wu Tingsheng with a capital of 100,000 yuan. The company collects British American Tobacco Company tobacco. Since the focus of this case is whether it involves foreign capital, if it is not foreign capital, please provide written certification. Shen Weiting believed that there was something difficult to do and did not agree to do so. Later, he provided a piece of paper declaring on behalf of the company that it was Chinese-owned. However, it was neither signed nor stamped with the association's seal, so it was not a formal and responsible document. Later, larger Chinese cigarette factories, such as Nanyang, Huacheng, and Fuxin, were asked separately, and they all said that they had not entrusted the Xuchang Company to collect tobacco leaves, nor had they invested capital in it. They also had doubts about the organization of the Xuchang Company. The Nanyang Company also stated that few Chinese businessmen agreed with the Xuchang Company and that many opposed it. The association's proposition could not represent all manufacturers. This matter is complex, and it is feared that foreign businesses will manipulate raw materials and public opinion with huge capital, making it impossible to discover the truth. Therefore, we should formally request your ministry to carefully investigate whether the company is nominally Chinese-owned but actually controlled by foreigners. This involves foreign businesses setting up factories in disguise in the interior. Once this precedent is set, treaties will be rendered meaningless, and the harm will be endless. We must strictly prevent this. According to the Nanyang Company, the Xuchang Company has close ties with local officials and gentry. This matter is related to your ministry's investigation policy, so we dare not fail to report the above.

The Legislative Yuan is Revising the Trademark Law. A Draft Has Been Prepared and Is Being Reviewed by the Commercial Law Committee. Director of the Trademark Bureau He Zhuoxian Was Summoned to Participate in the Discussion. 108

Since the issue of pictographic and homophonic trademarks caused disputes last year, the Legislative Yuan is now engaged in revising the Trademark Law, and a draft has been prepared. On the 3rd of this month, the Commercial Law Committee of the Legislative Yuan held a special meeting to discuss it. He Zhuoxian, the director of the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, was summoned to attend the meeting in Nanjing at that time. He returned to Shanghai yesterday after completing his official duties. According to him, speaking to a reporter from the New Voice News Agency, the revised draft is still under review. The Commercial Law Committee held a meeting a few days ago and discussed it in detail, but the content is not yet convenient to disclose for the time being. The authorities attach great importance to this matter, and it is understood that the Commercial Law Committee is specifically soliciting opinions from all parties. After compiling and reviewing them in the future, they will be submitted to the meeting for discussion and then formally passed by the plenary session of the Legislative Yuan.

Nanjing Road Citizens' First District Branch - Contributing Telephone Rate Increase Opinions - Reducing Spending is Better Than Increasing Rates - The Best Strategy to Preserve Interest 112

The Nanjing Road Citizens' First District Branch has repeatedly argued against the proposed telephone rate increase. At the beginning of the expert committee's visit, they already contributed opinions for reference. Now that the experts' research is nearing completion and the report and decisions are about to be drafted, there is deep concern that the committee members may not have thoroughly investigated and studied the situation, and may not fully understand the socio-economic conditions of our country. Therefore, they have again written to the experts, putting forward the reasons why reducing spending is a more effective way to preserve interest than increasing rates. The letter is excerpted below:

Respectfully, our branch previously addressed the Shanghai Telephone Company's rate increase issue, which the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession accepted the resolution of the ratepayers' meeting to appoint your esteemed committee to investigate and study. The merchants and residents of Shanghai are deeply gratified. Our branch submitted five key points to your esteemed committee on August 30 for reference. Recently, we learned that you gentlemen are not only thorough, but also widely solicit opinions from all parties before finalizing the report, which we admire for your humility and willingness to adopt good ideas. We noted that the Chinese Ratepayers Association sent a letter to your esteemed committee on September 16, stating that it had submitted a resolution to the Municipal Council to expand the scope of research, namely: (1) Whether the fixed rate of interest preservation is reasonable; (2) Whether operating income subsidies and material purchase commissions should be outside of operating expenses; (3) Whether there is a way to avoid exchange losses, and to which force this fault belongs, and whether it should be compensated by the public. In addition, several opinions were raised, such as the vast difference between the socio-economic levels of Shanghai and cities outside of China; China being a silver-using country, its currency unit value is much lower than that of gold-using countries, and cannot be compared; China's mechanization is different from Europe, America, and Japan, and has not yet reached the stage of familiarity; Chinese people are more frugal than gold-using countries, etc., all of which are extremely accurate and represent the desires of all users, and are worthy of consideration by your esteemed committee. Now, our branch has important opinions to supplement and state. The Shanghai Telephone Company's proposal to increase rates is solely based on the reason of preserving interest. However, according to the principles of economics, the lower the price, the more users there are, and the higher the price, the fewer users there are. The increase or decrease in the supply and demand of telephone services may also be difficult to violate this established rule. If the telephone company must implement a rate increase or charge per call, users will inevitably decrease rather than increase. Then "the desire to distribute interest" still cannot be maintained. Will this insufficient budget be added to the shoulders of the remaining users, endlessly cycling? Then the company's affairs will not have time to be considered, and thoughts and brains will be used all year round, isn't that a joke? Moreover, the market is indeed in its last throes, and is unusually depressed. Whether merchants or residents, they all consider reducing spending as the best strategy, and are determined not to increase unnecessary expenses. Why can't the telephone company abandon the plan to increase rates, and similarly adopt reducing spending as an effective method to preserve interest? We use this as a way to plan. We pray that you gentlemen will condescend to discuss it.
