"Fifth Fourth Mold" Correction 216

— Cao Juren

Yesterday, while flipping through Huang Yuansheng's posthumous works, I found the following record in his Confession:

"When I was a student at Nanxun Public School, ... students were talking about revolution, freedom, democracy and the like. We envied the students of Nanyang Public School for their school strike, which was praised by newspapers. We sent a telegram to congratulate them, which read: 'All students of Nanxun Public School congratulate all students of Nanyang Public School on their liberation from the suffering of autocratic schools.' It was printed in large letters and published in the Zhongwai Daily News. We also provoked a dispute with the school over a minor matter and went on strike as a whole, with me as the representative. After the strike, some students went to Shanghai to play, while others went to Nanyang Public School to take the entrance exam. At that time, the Public School was entirely government-run, and I was one of those who took the exam. In the past, I sent telegrams to congratulate others on their liberation from autocracy; now I am abandoning my own school of freedom and seeking a school of autocracy, which is not even obtainable. Without principles, without ideals, without integrity, I have been like this since I was young.

At that time, the student ethos regarded school strikes as a great achievement. After Nanyang Public School initiated it, remote rural areas were all affected. It spread overseas. Japanese students went on strike several times a year, and finally, the student affairs were resolved by suppressing the strike movement. Hu Hanmin was the strongest advocate of suppressing the strike movement, intending to use it as an opportunity for revolution. Wang Jingwei insisted that it was not possible and organized a maintenance association to resist it. Thinking about it now, revolutionaries are just magnified versions of the school strike movement."

This record is also unappealing. He exposes the scars of the student movement at the end of the Qing Dynasty too clearly. But why are student representatives so "without principles, without ideals, without integrity"? The reason deserves deep consideration. That is why I wanted to write the "Fifth Fourth Mold" random thoughts. I think intellectuals are the least reliable. They are certainly good at righteous indignation, but they are also the most likely to sell themselves for personal gain. Liang Qichao praised Yang Du as the most high-spirited young man, but he was the one who placed Yuan Shikai on the emperor's throne. Zhao Xinbo, the leader of the patriotic movement in Shanghai, is now the number one traitor. As Huang Yuansheng himself described, he himself was a student representative who was the first to take the entrance exam for the so-called "autocratic Nanyang Public School." The wandering consciousness of intellectuals is the most terrible. To portray the student representatives of the May Fourth Movement as pure social activists is the most dangerous. Intellectuals themselves will forget their own shadows of decline, and the general public will entrust all movements to intellectuals to lead. The old saying is still true: "Scholars rebel, and they will not succeed in three years." Very few student representatives are willing to serve society from beginning to end! I think we ourselves should admit our mistakes like Huang Yuansheng, expose our own malignant syphilis, and not use nice words to cover it up! Huang Yuansheng also said:

"In the age of science, I had no thoughts of becoming an official. When I was about to graduate as a student studying abroad, the thought of making a living and the so-called thought of loving the country clashed in my mind. From then on, it was a period of constant struggle between reason and desire. Reason did not prevail over desire, so I fell into depravity. Desire did not prevail over reason, so I suffered. The more I suffered, the more I fell into depravity, and the more I fell into depravity, the more I suffered. The two cycled and coexisted, disturbing me endlessly. ... The poison of poison, the ferocity of wild boars and long snakes, is still not as good as the officialdom of China. It kills talents, which is a sharp weapon. Shamelessness, depravity, ignorance, corruption, and all kinds of things are brewed and increased by it. It is a breeding ground for all evils. ... After the revolution, parties and associations were established in large numbers. What I regret most is the prevalence of the buying and selling of people during this period. Rogues of all kinds throughout the country are like pigs and cattle that have been labeled and put on the market. The small ones sell their skin and flesh, and the large ones sell everything, even their hair and bones. Among the three hundred women in the brothels, there are indeed some with charming appearances, but even women with yellow faces and ugly appearances are worth ten thousand dollars, with triple profits. It is like the meat market surging, even diseased pigs and cattle are walking without legs. In recent years, personality has been swept away."

——Confessions (Oriental Magazine, 1915)

His "sighs of grief" resonate with me. Zhou Liangong recorded that Ruan Dacheng's family's actor, Li, "died in Nanjing, and the actors were scattered in other rooms. The actor Li refused to perform the plays written by Huai Ning at the request of the guests, and he also asked his peers not to perform them. Asked why? He said: 'Even if my father's name is not mentioned, I can't avoid being talked about. Every time I perform his plays, the guests laugh and scold in every way, making people feel annoyed all day long. It is better to refuse and do good.'" Ruan Dacheng served Wei Zhongxian and became Wei's adopted son and godfather, which can be regarded as the most shameless of the literati at the end of the Ming Dynasty. The conduct of a great writer is not as bright and upright as that of an actor. Everyone, think about it, if intellectuals lead social movements, will those movements have good endings?

椥 217

— Menghua

Ever since I left the deck crowded with passengers (who can be said to be all compatriots who could not make a living in the country), I have been in a state of dizziness and resentment. The strangeness of a foreign country, the abuse of the white race, the equatorial sun, and the depressed mood really made me suffer enough. I did not feel relieved until I left Saigon.

This time, with the help of friends living in Saigon, I finally found a companion to go to Trà Vinh together. He was an old overseas Chinese who went to Siam at the age of eleven, and then from Siam to Java. He only came to Annam eleven years ago. Looking at his graying temples, I guessed he must be over forty. It was much better to have such a companion. On the way, we talked about stories that were like legends, adventure novels, and Tarzan-like stories. Because when he first arrived in Siam, it could be said to be a primitive world, so anyone who went to the tropics risked their lives to make a fortune. And he was also a brave man who risked his life. Does the old man keep shaking his head when he speaks? He seemed overwhelmed with emotion. This is also inevitable. After running around for several decades, others have already become wealthy gentlemen, but he still only has a bamboo basket and a scarf. According to himself, he lost his fortune due to gambling, so he must have made a fortune at least.

I will not forget the night I arrived in Trà Vinh. The tropical sunset was really even more gorgeous. I have seen the sunset over the Yellow River, the sunset over Mount Tai, and the setting sun over Lake Tai, but this place is completely different. The Yellow River is tragic, Mount Tai is far and wide, and you can see the distant and low clouds in the west, and you can also see the darkness in the east, which is a foil for the magnificent fire. Lake Tai, on the other hand, is a vast expanse of water with a colorful cloud floating on it, which is distant and charming. But this place, apart from the towering trees and coconut groves, is hot and empty, and there is also a depressing atmosphere.

The next day, at a little after four o'clock, I joined the unfamiliar team and set off for Sóc Trăng. Sóc Trăng is called one of the six provinces of Annam, but it is actually just a market town in a village, so the surroundings are particularly clean and refreshing, and there is a different flavor compared to Saigon. After arriving at the school, I liked to sit at the door, where I could see the coconut groves, blue sky, and white clouds on the opposite bank. At dusk, the stars were like the tips of needles, too small to get used to seeing, and too bright to get used to seeing. Really, I have arrived in a very different place.

The Cultivation of Dependence 218

— Yi

The Story of a Horse (Part 2) 219

— Lin Shi

On the mountain in early spring, some branches are still bare, some have sprouted green leaves, and some are evergreen, still looking dark green, just not as oily black as in summer. Azaleas have not yet bloomed, but they have also formed small buds. Its hooves felt soft and tender on the delicate grass, although not as thickly felted as in summer. Only the birds, flying freely in the forest, raised their voices and called out vigorously.

Walking around in the forest, the master still refused to get off its back. The gray dog, however, was sniffing around in the bushes, trying to smell out the scent of rabbits or other wild animals. Soon, the dog walked forward sniffing the ground, barking spiritually. The master understood that this meant it had discovered the scent of a wild animal. So the master directed it to follow behind the dog. Walking, walking, turning from this mountain depression to that mountain depression. Sure enough, the dog was searching for a rabbit. The rabbit desperately tried to escape, and the dog chased closely behind. At this time, the master's muscles were tense with joy, as if he saw a large lump of gold rolling in front of him, rolling, about to fall into the sea. He had to fly over and pick it up as quickly as if he were shooting an arrow, otherwise his wealth would be lost forever, and it would be gone without a trace. The master whipped it on its back, and it was excruciatingly painful. So it had to follow the dog quickly, watching from afar as the rabbit frantically fled for its life, running with quick hops. Suddenly, a gunshot rang in its ears, and it couldn't help but jump in fright. It saw the rabbit fall to the ground in response, twitching slightly in the grass. Then the dog nimbly ran over and picked it up, delivering it spiritedly to its master, grunting in its throat. Only the rabbit's bright red blood dripped to the ground, dyeing the green grass crimson.

The horse was chilled by this cruel moment, and then stared blankly at the corpse with its eyes closed, motionless, and at the blood congealed on the grass. It thought: This rabbit, not long ago, it was moving freely in the mountains and forests. It did not invade anyone, it was living without causing harm, eating small grass and tender leaves when it was hungry. Maybe in that stone cave, it also had its home, maybe it still had newborn children waiting for it to return. But ah, before it encountered this disaster, it would not have thought that it would die soon, and it did not want to die! Then why did it have to die? Did it commit a capital crime simply by living without causing harm? Who would pronounce its death sentence? Oh! The master is so greedy, and so savage and cruel! But it really couldn't understand: why was the dog also so cruel? If it is said that the human master is cruel, then isn't the dog also not human? Then it thought: it was not without sin for the innocent death of this rabbit, although it was not it that fired the gun, nor was it itself looking for its tracks, but if it had endured the master's whipping at that time, and had not run so fast, maybe the bullet would not have hit the rabbit's body, maybe it would have had a chance to escape home and meet the children waiting for it.——This kind of self-condemnation made the horse very uncomfortable, it seemed to see the rabbit's eyes wide open in anger demanding its life. It lowered its head in terror, and saw the blood on the grass again, a thick stench piercing the depths of its nose, so it closed its eyelids tightly, as if it were about to faint.

After a while, the horse heard the master laughing heartily, as if he was overjoyed. Obviously, the corpse and blood did not move him in any way. Then he said loudly to the dog:

"Okay, let's do another one. Rabbit meat is very fresh. Take it back, I'll eat it, and I'll give you some to eat."

Sure enough, the dog barked twice more, and joyfully plunged into the bushes, and went to offer his skills to his master again. But soon after, when the dog found the rabbit again, the horse immediately thought: maybe this is the son of the one who was just killed, it came out to look for its mother who had not yet returned, would it have to watch it follow its mother and be brutally killed by the ferocious master? No, I must not let it be like this. With all my strength, I must preserve its free life.——So when the master whipped it again to chase forward, it was angry for justice, it roared, leapt, and used all its strength to throw the master off its back and onto the ground. And it ran forward, caught up with the dog, and trampled the dog hard on the ground, so that it could not get up anyway, so that the poor rabbit could escape, escape to a very far place, escape to its stone cave home.

This, of course, made the master very angry. When it was forced back home by the master, its body had been beaten with many wounds, bleeding, like the blood flowing out of the dead rabbit. It was hungry and thirsty, and the master would not give it water to drink, nor would he give it straw to eat. After being hungry for a long time, it thought how delicious the dry straw would be.

Looking in from the veranda, it saw the master with a white cloth wrapped around his head--that was for the injuries it had caused--chewing on rabbit meat, eating it with relish and oil all over his mouth.

Late at night, the horse was tightly tied in the stable. Still there was not a drop of water or a blade of grass. It was tired, but also tired of thinking. Everything during the day was clearly remembered in its mind. The master's always poisonous treatment of it would not make it forget. This is too obvious: it served the master loyally all its life, but the reward it received was endless whipping. In any case, this small stable was not a place for it to settle down, and at the same time it was no longer willing to submit to the whip to get a few leather strips to eat.

The night was so quiet, not a sound could be heard, like a tomb. The surrounding darkness tightly wrapped it, and there was not even the possibility of free breathing. But it was sure that even though it was old, it would still have to live. It missed how wide and big the world in the mountains and forests was, it missed how bright the spring sun was, it missed how tender and fat the green grass in the fields was, and it missed how smooth the air in the forest was. So it gnawed at the rope that bound its head, its breathing hurried.

After a long time, the tightly bound rope finally broke. Looking out from the small window, the sky was already dawning at this time. The old horse strained and broke through the plank wall of the stable, and then broke through the bamboo fence of the courtyard. It had never been so excited. It forgot its thirst and forgot its hunger. Its whole body was roaring with strength, roaring loudly, shattering the silent sky. In the dim morning light, it jumped and ran into the forest.

Prison Van 220

— Dabao

Stepping onto the carriage door,

Still stretching his head to look at the street scene,

Is it the fear of death,

Or the attachment to life?

The carriage door closed,

Leaving only the clanking of shackles resounding in the darkness,

Dizzying in front of his eyes.

Dozing off, he rehashed the past,

His broken heart,

Began to float with black fantasies...

Like entering an ice room,

He began to feel cold all over.

The death penalty would soon declare the end of the world for him,

Lowering his head, he imagined the opening scene of the next life...

A shock, announcing that the prison van was about to depart,

He raised his head,

Through the iron window, he glanced at the human world for the last time...

Honorable Old Woman (4) 221

— By Emashu, translated by Ren Jun

Her son was congratulated by the people of the town and sent off with lively fanfare, as he went to fulfill his military service—the people of our hometown had to go to a neighboring place to join the army. The old woman made quite a commotion, tearfully following her son for about two li of the road.

Now, only the old woman herself and her husband remained at home. The husband had been bedridden like a cripple for ten years due to his epilepsy.

The old woman's fidelity to this troublesome husband, whose temper had been soured by his chronic illness, had always been well-known. Not only that, but it was also a source of great pride for the old woman. We do not know if she loved her husband. However, at the very least, it is true that she felt the obligation of being a wife from the bottom of her heart. In reality, ten years is by no means a short period of time. During this time, she would work part-time at my home, and would devote all her rest time in the early morning and evening to the care of the patient. And, of course, she would often talk proudly about her fidelity; yet without any complaints. My mother, being deeply sympathetic to this situation, often praised her. At such times, she felt comforted from the bottom of her heart, and tears flowed non-stop.

Although there is a saying that "women are useless things," at the same time they are also the kind of creatures who cannot avoid being sentimental. One evening, a young man working in my factory actually started making advances towards the old woman. Perhaps she was not angry, but the next morning she hurriedly ran to my mother and told her about the young man's misconduct in every detail.

"No matter how useless the patient is, a husband is still a husband. I am also a proper woman with a husband. – I said this while yelling at that guy, isn't that right, Madam!"

"Of course, of course, you are an admirable person. I will also call that guy over and give him a good scolding." Only with great difficulty did my mother persuade her to go back.

Afterward, my mother smiled and said to the people beside her:

"Ah, the old woman is also a woman. Until now, she has never thought about that matter even once..."

Special Edition of Shen Bao

Talk

The Struggle for Open Doors 222

— Hang An

What are the world powers fighting for? In a nutshell, it is the open door of colonies and semi-colonies. Originally, due to the result of overproduction, imperialism had only one way to solve its domestic economic problems, and that was to expand outward. Thus, the open door of colonies and semi-colonies became a must-have for them. And the world has become troubled by this matter.

According to a United China News Agency dispatch from Tokyo on the 1st, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs is now actively preparing to break the deadlock in Anglo-Japanese diplomacy. When British economic expert Sir Ross visited Japan, he had a series of earnest talks with Foreign Minister Hirota. Ambassador Matsudaira, who returned from London, and Commercial Counselor Matsuyama also held final discussions with Foreign Minister Hirota, deciding to demand that Britain open the doors of its colonies, allow the development of Japanese commerce, and declare to Britain that if Britain cannot open its doors to the world, then please do not shout the slogan of opening the doors of East Asia in the future, and only by allowing Japan to move into British territories can Anglo-Japanese cooperation be implemented in the world.

This is the Anglo-Japanese dispute. What Britain is fighting for is the open door of East Asia, and what Japan is fighting for is the open door of British colonies. The open door of East Asia was originally open. Since September 18th, Britain has gradually been forced out, so it cannot remain silent. As for the open door of British colonies, Japan has recently invaded with a dumping policy. But it has been severely hit due to Britain's resistance. Because of this, Japan is using Britain's desire to restore its rights and interests in the Far East as an opportunity to demand that it open the doors of its territories as a price for exchange. Whether Anglo-Japanese cooperation can succeed in the future depends on whether the two countries' market competition can find a compromise.

According to a Havas dispatch from London on the 1st, the American branch of the International Women's League for Peace and Freedom held a meeting at Conway Hall last night. Ms. Doherty Sertzer gave a speech saying that the United States has recently completed the construction of eighty-six new warships, and the reason is that there will be a day when these warships will be needed in the Far East. This also shows the determination of the United States to fight for the open door in the Far East. The eighty-six new warships that the United States has recently completed are to meet the needs of this action.

Here, we can see the seriousness of the Far East issue. However, what will China, the center of the issue, do with its own open door?

A Trembling Hand 223

— Jin Ma

Every time, every time, when I suffocatingly crawl down from my cramped and dark attic room, just like a pigeon coop, and slip out the back door into that dim and narrow alley; a withered, banana-peel-colored, trembling hand comes into my view. Slowly, slowly approaching, approaching: moving close to my waist, and then trembling even more fiercely.

This is an old man, a crippled old man with only one leg and one hand left: tattered clothes, a tattered face, tattered yellow hair, already make people immediately feel that this is not a person. But a, a what? I can't say. Like a garbage dump? A garbage dump overflowing with an odor so filthy it makes one want to vomit! However, he is still a life, a human life like myself!

I dare not look at him anymore. The first time that trembling hand moved over, I could still take the coppers for buying steamed buns out of my pocket and give them to him, satisfying his hope. But after that, every time, I also slipped out the back door with a body full of hunger and cold, or still walked back to the house with even more hunger and cold disappointment. The old man's trembling hand could no longer get any favor from me.

Once, it was a morning presenting all the liveliness of a bustling city, but it was quietly drizzling plum rain, blowing a bone-chilling autumn wind. When I, with a gloomy heart, listlessly wandered into that alley, which seemed even gloomier, that trembling hand appeared before my eyes again. This kind of annoying sight almost made me feel angry immediately. I walked with my head down, feeling dejected, but that trembling hand seemed to be connected to me by an invisible thread, still only about a foot away, following, following.

The alley was long and narrow; I quickened my pace a little, but that trembling hand also closely followed my pace. Turning a corner, I stopped, standing there motionless, staring at that

Page 18

drawing of turtles fighting painted with chalk on the wall and the faded advertisement for injecting Salvarsan 606. And the trembling hand was moving closer, almost as if it were going to grab my pocket. Although I knew there was nothing in my pocket, I could no longer calm down, annoyance filled my whole being, I hatefully glared at him—

"What do you want?"

And what answered me was that the hand trembled even more fiercely.

I ignored him; I turned the corner and walked straight towards the back door of my house. Just as my foot was about to step over the threshold; a trembling, weak, tiny sound, almost like the buzzing of a fly, floated into my ear—

"Sir!"

I immediately knew it was that annoying old fellow again. When I turned around to look, that trembling hand appeared in my view again.

I helplessly shook my head, my hand instinctively stuffed into my pocket at this moment, the pocket was empty, only fumbling out a token from the "hot water shop." He looked at my hand holding the token in disappointment, and somehow it started to tremble too.

Nine Plates 224

— Especially

According to the old custom, I wiped my face and ate a bowl of rice porridge.

Originally, Tie always got up very early, but what about today? I didn't see him come out. In order to hurry on the road, I woke him up from the back room. Something was off; his complexion was not good, eye mucus filling the corners of his eyes, and the smile on his lips was not very natural. Yesterday's diarrhea had made things difficult for him.

I couldn't worry about so much; we still had to set off.

The porter always liked to mingle with us, talking about this and that, telling us many things we had never heard, but today, he also seemed a little unhappy, his mouth closed, his head constantly lowered, as if he were thinking about something. Perhaps, he was not feeling well? I thought, but I didn't feel comfortable asking him.

The mountain road was not felt to be a hardship when walking in our large group. Ten li was nothing rare; in the blink of an eye, we arrived at the entrance of Suosuo Beach, ten li straight from Zhengzhi Street.

"Should we take a boat or walk?" the old porter asked.

"How would we take a boat? How would we walk?"

"If we take a boat, we can row twenty li on the water, starting from here, passing Snake Skin Beach, Coffin Rock, all the way to Xie's Street. If we walk, we can take this mountain path to Xie's Street as well."

"Which is better, taking a boat or walking?" Old Tie asked bluntly.

"That all depends on what the guests prefer; either way is fine."

The bank of the beach water was more than ten feet high; the bank was planted with locust trees. The poisonous sun seemed to scorch the dense thickets. Several cicadas were screeching desperately, not feeling any wind; the air only brought signs of sultry heat.

Casually walking on the bank for a while, the water was so clear, you could see the bottom, the green moss and swimming fish clearly moving before your eyes. The waves, gliding over from the endless end, made me realize that taking a boat would be dangerous against the current, and it would not be convenient for travelers.

After considering it, I decided to give up the idea of taking a boat, raised the banner of the vanguard, and proceeded under the scorching sun.

At first, the porters still revealed a layer of hopeful expressions, telling you in their expressions how much they hoped to adopt the first route, but they didn't dare to say it. In their eyes, how much passionate light was contained! Finally, the light retreated, and a gray gloom fell upon their hearts.

By the time we reached Taigongpu, the sun was already setting a bit. We had a quick meal, filled our stomachs, and saw that it was time to go, but none of the porters could be seen. Thus, we were delayed for twenty or thirty minutes. Later, a porter finally found them from some opium den.

"Something's not right; look at the faces of the two old porters, Lao Zhang and Lao Liu, they look even worse," I said to Tie.

"Why is that? Is it because they had a feast?"

"You're asking me? Who knows."

After setting off, we were all worried, a common understanding arising from the bottom of our hearts, as if something was about to happen and something terrible was about to occur. We were very quiet, not making a sound in our mouths, silently listening to the beating of our hearts.

"Strange, why aren't the porters chanting their jargon either?" A heavy stone pressed on my chest, preventing me from taking a breath.

Roughly estimating that we had passed another five or six li, the trees on the mountain were even denser. If a few people were ambushed, it would not be easy to see. The distance between the stone steps seemed to be a little higher than before, and more corroded.

"Quietly, don't be arrogant, the Nine Plates ahead are very dangerous!" The young porter Liu hurriedly said only this sentence and hurriedly left. (To be continued)

Song of the River 225

— Ye Ge

The river water rages, the waves like an angry giant stir up the air, hoping to crash against the shore. It crashes against the rocks, shrieking sharply, and then shatters into countless white foam, splashing in the clear morning sky.

Far away along the upper reaches, riding the crest of a wave, a barge rushes over like flying. In front of it, a small sampan is bouncing up and down with the waves. On the sampan stands a young fellow, a piece of black cloth tied around his head, gently fluttering in the breeze, wearing a short black jacket, his two hands hurriedly rowing the oars. From time to time, he raises his head to look at the sky, the soft sunlight making him furrow his brow, and then lowers it to look at the turbulent waves on the river before turning his head to smile at an old man on the barge.

The old man sits leisurely at the stern, holding the rudder, sometimes also raising his head to smile at the young man, and at other times, indulging in sweet memories. The waves violently surge, and the sampan leaps and jumps, the young man busily and hurriedly rowing the oars, then turns his head to the barge again and smiles softly:

"Old man, you're entranced!"

The old man angrily raises his head, gives him a stern look, and then sinks back into beautiful contemplation.

The young man laughs to himself twice, suddenly feeling bored; then he raises his voice, imitating the tone of an adult, and sings loudly in rhythm with his labor:

"The river water surges, the sound of the boat bumping, it's the tide!...

The old man on the boat suddenly coughs loudly, followed by two or three yawns in quick succession. The young man closes his mouth, turns his head, and cunningly laughs loudly: "Old man, you're entranced, you're dazed!"

The old man angrily shouts and waves his hand: "Go to hell!"

The young man smiles contentedly, turns his head, faces the river, and pulls the oars twice, and then continues to sing:

"Waves carry love, the sea buries gold..."

A gust of wind blows close, bringing a general damp chill, the young man opens his mouth wide and yawns a few times, saliva flying into the sky and falling on the river. Then he turns his head again, peering with his rat-like eyes, and shouts at the old man as if provoking him:

"Old man, I say what are you entranced by, how can you be so dull..." The old man this time isn't angry, he smiles amiably:

"Little rascal, be careful or I'll tear out your tongue later!"

The young man puts on a ghostly face, pretends to be anxious, sticks out his tongue, and pats his chest with his hand, saying:

"Oh dear, how can that be! If you tear out my tongue, I won't be able to sing for you, old man..."

The river water rages again, the waves stretch out their tongues, pushing the sampan high and then dropping it down, the young man angrily clenches his teeth and rows the oars with force, then continues to sing:

"The sun sinks on the horizon, old geese encounter cold sounds, but what about the fish?... Hidden deep in the water..."

The old man stands up suddenly, the breeze on the river blows his silver-white beard, he stares blankly with his sharp eyes, looking at the clear morning sky; then he smiles slightly and sits down again.

The young man still wants to sing at the top of his voice, a wave suddenly crashes on his sampan, the sampan starts to sway, he angrily rows the oars, muttering curses. The old man strokes his silver-white beard and shouts loudly:

"Almost to shore!" The young man raises his head to look and then sings on in a mumbling voice.

Recent News from the New Generation 231

— Qian

Tang Jie eats tree bark - Mr. Tang Jie, in "Mr. Wang Goes to the Countryside" returned to his hometown to cultivate. He encountered a drought, and the villagers were in a state of great distress. Yesterday, he photographed the famine victims eating grass roots, followed by tree bark. Mr. Wang's family all ate tree bark to fill their hunger. Mr. Wang couldn't swallow it and was in great pain, it is said.

Cao Xuesong becomes a committee member - In Mr. Wang's friend Xiao Chen's hometown, after the drought, a famine followed. There were dead bodies in the wild, and no surplus food in the rooms. The disaster was serious and the situation was unbearable to witness. The couple Xiao Chen and Cao Xuesong are charitable and very enthusiastic about public welfare. This time, in response to the invitation of the Drought Relief Association, they have been honored to be appointed as members of the relief distribution committee, and will soon arrive in their hometown to distribute relief, it is said.

Zuo Ming goes to the countryside - Zuo Ming, who played the word-splitting gentleman in "Mr. Wang in Secret" and the small loser in "Mr. Wang's New Year", had few scenes, but his acting was excellent. However, because there were few scenes, he was never publicly credited. This time, in "Mr. Wang Goes to the Countryside", there is a role of a friend who flatters, the position in the play is very important. Zuo Ming volunteered to play the role and achieved excellent results. It can be predicted.

Huang Naishuang refuses marriage - Xiao A Yuan Huang Naishuang, played a farm girl in "Mr. Wang Goes to the Countryside", innocent, lively and lovely. The local bully Zhu Dade coveted her beauty, entrusted someone to be a matchmaker, but it was not successful. Then he went to propose marriage himself, but unexpectedly was rejected by Xiao A Yuan. Yesterday, when filming this scene, Huang Naishuang's performance of rejecting the marriage was extremely vivid and lifelike. Viewers praised her endlessly.

Star News 232

"Emerald Horse" is a successful work for which Xu Xinfu has racked his brains. The whole play is full of danger and surprise, and it is the first Chinese sound detective blockbuster. It has now been completed and is expected to cause a sensation on the day of its release.

Shen Xiling's masterpiece after "Nostalgia" is "Boat Girl", which has now been completed. It was recently test-screened at the Central Theater, and the results were excellent. It is expected that its release will definitely refresh the audience's eyes and ears.

The location shooting team of "Peach Blossoms After the Robbery", written by Hong Shen and directed by Zhang Shichuan, returned to Shanghai a few days ago after completing all the work. The stage work is now beginning.

Mr. Zhengqiu's posthumous work "Brothers" is jointly directed by Cheng Bugao and Zheng Xiaoqiu, and work has now begun.

The long-rumored new film "Tuberose" has been staged at the Shanghai Xinguang Theater.

Silver Miscellany 233

— Zhier

Chen Gong Jiazhen’s "compiled and photographed" collection of movie star photos, the third issue "Bathing Suit Issue," the cover is again "Diao Ban Hua's Bathing Photo." Very beautiful; it seems destined that foes will meet.

Some say: This is Chen Gong's early work (presumably the copper plates were also prepared long ago). If it were now, Chen Gong would certainly not be like this, and Diao Gong would not be either. Is that so?

Mr. Mu Shiying had a "refutation of rumors" in the Social Daily on the 6th, saying that he had only met Wang Ying three times, and the "last time" was when he "secretly fled the gathering"; from pursuing Wang Ying, he concluded: "As for me, in my short twenty-four years of life, I seem not to have easily pursued anyone, nor have I ever had a failed pursuit."

I think Mr. Ye Lingbao should also write a letter refuting the rumor that he never pursued Wang Ying, and publish it somewhere (or write a long article, which may be titled "The Beginning and End of Me and Wang Ying"), because this troublesome and old-fashioned rumor has become more and more widespread recently, and Mr. Mu's "refutation of rumors" also involves Mr. Ye.

Publishing World 234

Recently, Paramount's export, the film "The Crusades" directed by the great director Cecil B. DeMille, caused a sensation in Shanghai, because of the film's great plot and astonishing cost, so many people rushed to see it. It is now heard that the Movie Star Photo Agency at 138 Nanjing Road, Shanghai, has "The Crusades" stills for sale, with one set containing four sheets, representing the four most exciting scenes in the entire film, each set selling for only one dime, hence the exceptionally brisk sales in recent days. In addition, Shirley Temple's photos are particularly popular, and they are sold at the stationery department of Wing On Company on Nanjing Road, Shanghai.
